       </tr>
      </table>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Flora_and_fauna">
        Flora and fauna
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Red_eyed_tree_frog_edit2.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1720" data-file-width="2293" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Red_eyed_tree_frog_edit2.jpg/220px-Red_eyed_tree_frog_edit2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Red_eyed_tree_frog_edit2.jpg/330px-Red_eyed_tree_frog_edit2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Red_eyed_tree_frog_edit2.jpg/440px-Red_eyed_tree_frog_edit2.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Red_eyed_tree_frog_edit2.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Red-eyed Tree Frog (
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Agalychnis_callidryas" title="Agalychnis callidryas">
           Agalychnis callidryas
          </a>
         </i>
         )
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HeliconiusDorisLinnaeus.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="649" data-file-width="1000" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/HeliconiusDorisLinnaeus.jpg/220px-HeliconiusDorisLinnaeus.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/HeliconiusDorisLinnaeus.jpg/330px-HeliconiusDorisLinnaeus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/HeliconiusDorisLinnaeus.jpg/440px-HeliconiusDorisLinnaeus.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HeliconiusDorisLinnaeus.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <i>
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heliconius_doris" title="Heliconius doris">
           Heliconius doris
          </a>
         </i>
         Linnaeus butterfly of Costa Rica
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Costa_Rica" title="Wildlife of Costa Rica">
        Wildlife of Costa Rica
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Costa Rica is home to a rich variety of plants and animals. While the country has only about 0.03% of the world's landmass, it contains 5% of the world's
       <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">
        biodiversity
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian07_59-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Guardian07-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Honey99_60-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Honey99-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Around 25% of the country's land area is in protected national parks and protected areas,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
        <a href="#cite_note-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the largest percentage of protected areas in the world (developing world average 13%, developed world average 8%).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI1_63-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ODI1-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
        <a href="#cite_note-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
        <a href="#cite_note-65">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Costa Rica has successfully managed to diminish
       <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">
        deforestation
       </a>
       from some of the worst rates in the world from 1973 to 1989, to almost zero by 2005.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI1_63-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ODI1-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       One national park, the
       <a href="/wiki/Corcovado_National_Park" title="Corcovado National Park">
        Corcovado National Park
       </a>
       , is internationally renowned among ecologists for its biodiversity (including
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Big_cats" title="Big cats">
        big cats
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tapirs" title="Tapirs">
        tapirs
       </a>
       ) and is where visitors can expect to see an abundance of wildlife.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
        <a href="#cite_note-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
        <a href="#cite_note-67">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Corcovado is the one park in Costa Rica where
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Costa_Rican_monkey_species" title="List of Costa Rican monkey species">
        all four Costa Rican monkey species
       </a>
       can be found.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-watching_68-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-watching-68">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
       These include the
       <a href="/wiki/White-headed_capuchin" title="White-headed capuchin">
        white-headed capuchin
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Mantled_howler" title="Mantled howler">
        mantled howler
       </a>
       , the endangered
       <a href="/wiki/Geoffroy%27s_spider_monkey" title="Geoffroy's spider monkey">
        Geoffroy's spider monkey
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-watching_68-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-watching-68">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
        <a href="#cite_note-69">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Central_American_squirrel_monkey" title="Central American squirrel monkey">
        Central American squirrel monkey
       </a>
       , found only on the Pacific coast of Costa Rica and a small part of
       <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">
        Panama
       </a>
       , and considered endangered until 2008, when its status was upgraded to vulnerable.
       <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">
        Deforestation
       </a>
       , illegal pet-trading, and hunting are the main reasons for its threatened status.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
        <a href="#cite_note-70">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Tortuguero_National_Park" title="Tortuguero National Park">
        Tortuguero National Park
       </a>
       – the name
       <i>
        Tortuguero
       </i>
       can be translated as "Full of Turtles" – is home to spider, howler, and white-throated capuchin monkeys; the
       <a href="/wiki/Three-toed_sloth" title="Three-toed sloth">
        three-toed sloth
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Two-toed_sloth" title="Two-toed sloth">
        two-toed sloth
       </a>
       ; 320 species of birds; and a variety of reptiles. The park is recognized for the annual nesting of the endangered
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Green_turtle" title="Green turtle">
        green turtle
       </a>
       , and is the most important nesting site for the species. Giant
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leatherback_turtle" title="Leatherback turtle">
        leatherback
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hawksbill_turtle" title="Hawksbill turtle">
        hawksbill
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Loggerhead_Sea_Turtle" title="Loggerhead Sea Turtle">
        loggerhead
       </a>
       turtles also nest there. The
       <a href="/wiki/Monteverde_Cloud_Forest_Reserve" title="Monteverde Cloud Forest Reserve">
        Monteverde Cloud Forest Reserve
       </a>
       is home to about 2,000 plant species,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-karttv_71-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-karttv-71">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
       including numerous orchids. Over 400 types of birds and more than 100 species of mammals can be found there.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-karttv_71-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-karttv-71">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Over 840 species of birds have been identified in Costa Rica. As is the case in much of Central America, the avian species in Costa Rica are a mix of North and South American species. The country's abundant fruit trees, many of which bear fruit year round, are hugely important to the birds, some of whom survive on diets that consist only of one or two types of fruit. Some of the country's most notable avian species include the
       <a href="/wiki/Resplendent_quetzal" title="Resplendent quetzal">
        resplendent quetzal
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Scarlet_macaw" title="Scarlet macaw">
        scarlet macaw
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Three-wattled_bellbird" title="Three-wattled bellbird">
        three-wattled bellbird
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bare-necked_umbrellabird" title="Bare-necked umbrellabird">
        bare-necked umbrellabird
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/Keel-billed_toucan" title="Keel-billed toucan">
        keel-billed toucan
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
        <a href="#cite_note-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Instituto_Nacional_de_Biodiversidad" title="Instituto Nacional de Biodiversidad">
        Instituto Nacional de Biodiversidad
       </a>
       is allowed to collect royalties on any biological discoveries of medical importance. Costa Rica is a center of biological diversity for reptiles and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amphibians" title="Amphibians">
        amphibians
       </a>
       , including the world's fastest running lizard, the spiny-tailed iguana (
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Ctenosaura_similis" title="Ctenosaura similis">
         Ctenosaura similis
        </a>
       </i>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Garland1984_73-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Garland1984-73">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div style="clear:both;">
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Rivers">
        Rivers
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_rivers_of_Costa_Rica" title="List of rivers of Costa Rica">
        List of rivers of Costa Rica
       </a>
      </div>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
        Economy
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Intel_Costa_12_2007_SJO_105b.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="747" data-file-width="1120" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Intel_Costa_12_2007_SJO_105b.jpg/220px-Intel_Costa_12_2007_SJO_105b.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Intel_Costa_12_2007_SJO_105b.jpg/330px-Intel_Costa_12_2007_SJO_105b.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Intel_Costa_12_2007_SJO_105b.jpg/440px-Intel_Costa_12_2007_SJO_105b.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Intel_Costa_12_2007_SJO_105b.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         An
         <a href="/wiki/Intel" title="Intel">
          Intel
         </a>
         microprocessor facility in Costa Rica that was, at one time, responsible for 20% of Costa Rican exports and 5% of the country's GDP.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Costa_Rica" title="Economy of Costa Rica">
        Economy of Costa Rica
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The country has been considered economically stable with moderate inflation, estimated at 2.6% in 2017,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gfmag.com_74-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-gfmag.com-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and moderately high growth in GDP, which increased from US$41.3 billion in 2011 to US$52.6 billion in 2015.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-focus-economics.com_75-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-focus-economics.com-75">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The estimated GDP for 2017 is US$61.5 billion and the estimated GDP per capita (purchasing power parity) is US$12,382.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gfmag.com_74-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-gfmag.com-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The growing
       <a href="/wiki/Debt" title="Debt">
        debt
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Budget_deficit" title="Budget deficit">
        budget deficit
       </a>
       are the country's primary concerns.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_10-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       That is a primary reason why the major credit rating agencies –
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Standard_%26_Poor%E2%80%99s" title="Standard &amp; Poor’s">
        Standard &amp; Poor’s
       </a>
       , Moody’s and
       <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Fitch" title="Fitch">
        Fitch
       </a>
       – have downgraded Costa Rica’s risk ratings. For example,
       <a href="/wiki/Moody%27s_Investors_Service" title="Moody's Investors Service">
        Moody's Investors Service
       </a>
       in early 2017 reduced the rating to Ba2 from Ba1, with a negative outlook due to the "rising government debt burden and persistently high fiscal deficit, which was 5.2% of GDP in 2016" and the "lack of political consensus to implement measures to reduce the fiscal deficit [which] will result in further pressure on the government's
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Debt_ratios&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Debt ratios (page does not exist)">
        debt ratios
       </a>
       ".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
        <a href="#cite_note-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The country is currently debating major fiscal reform legislation to cut the budget deficits and stop the growth in debt,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_2-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-CIA-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       one of the highest in Latin America.
      </p>
      <p>
       Many foreign companies (manufacturing and services) operate in Costa Rica's Free Trade Zones (FTZ) where they benefit from investment and tax incentives.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cinde.org_9-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-cinde.org-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Well over half of that type of investment has come from the U.S.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
        <a href="#cite_note-77">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
       According to the government, the zones supported over 82 thousand direct jobs and 43 thousand indirect jobs in 2015.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_78-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Companies with facilities in the America Free Zone in Heredia, for example, include Intel, Dell, HP, Bayer, Bosch, DHL, IBM and Okay Industries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
        <a href="#cite_note-79">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
        <a href="#cite_note-80">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Of the GDP, 5.5% is generated by agriculture, 18.6% by industry and 75.9% by services.(2016)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gfmag.com_74-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-gfmag.com-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Agriculture employs 12.9% of the labor force, industry 18.57%, services 69.02% (2016)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-statista.com_81-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-statista.com-81">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
       For the region, its unemployment level is moderately high (8.2% in 2016, according to the IMF).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gfmag.com_74-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-gfmag.com-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Although 20.5% of the population lives below the poverty line (2017),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
        <a href="#cite_note-82">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Costa Rica has one of the highest standards of living in Central America.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
        <a href="#cite_note-83">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       High quality health care is provided by the government at low cost to the users.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
        <a href="#cite_note-84">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Housing is also very affordable. Costa Rica is recognized in Latin America for the quality of its educational system. Because of its educational system, Costa Rica has one of the highest literacy rates in Latin America, 97%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2016.export.gov_85-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-2016.export.gov-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
       General Basic Education is mandatory and provided without cost to the user.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
        <a href="#cite_note-86">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A US government report confirms that the country has "historically placed a high priority on education and the creation of a skilled work force" but notes that the high school drop-out rate is increasing. As well, Costa Rica would benefit from more courses in languages such as English, Portuguese, Mandarin and French and also in Science, Technology, Engineering and Math (STEM).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2016.export.gov_85-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-2016.export.gov-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Debt_and_deficit_issues">
        Debt and deficit issues
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">
        International Monetary Fund
       </a>
       stated in June 2017 that annual growth in the economy was just over 4% and that the financial system was sound.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
        <a href="#cite_note-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-imf.org_88-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-imf.org-88">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The IMF expressed concern however, about increasing
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Budget_deficit" title="Budget deficit">
        deficits
       </a>
       and public
       <a href="/wiki/Debt" title="Debt">
        debt
       </a>
       as well as the heavy dollarization of bank assets and liabilities. Costa Rica's public debt is problematic, especially as a percentage of the GDP, increasing from 29.8% in 2011 to 40.8% in 2015.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-focus-economics.com_75-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-focus-economics.com-75">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Of the proposed 2017 budget (US$15.9 billion), debt payments account for one-third of the total and a full 46% of the budget will require financing. That will increase the deficit and the debt owed to foreign entities.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
        <a href="#cite_note-89">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The value of the Costa Rican colone per US$1 was 526.46₡ on March 27, 2015. At the end of July 2017, the value was 563₡.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
        <a href="#cite_note-90">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
        <a href="#cite_note-91">
         [91]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
        <a href="#cite_note-92">
         [92]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       A 2017 study by the Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development warned that reducing the foreign debt must be a very high priority for the government. Other fiscal reforms were also recommended to moderate the budget deficit.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-news.co.cr_13-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-news.co.cr-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The IMF also recommended debt reduction, with specific suggestions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-imf.org_88-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-imf.org-88">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Liquidity_crisis">
        Liquidity crisis
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       In early August 2017, President
       <a href="/wiki/Luis_Guillermo_Sol%C3%ADs" title="Luis Guillermo Solís">
        Luis Guillermo Solís
       </a>
       admitted that the country was facing a "liquidity crisis" and promised that a higher VAT tax and higher income tax rates were being considered by his government. Such steps are essential, Luis Guillermo Solís told the nation, because it was facing difficulties in paying its obligations and guaranteeing the provision of services."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
        <a href="#cite_note-93">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Solís explained that the Treasury will prioritize payments on the public debt first, then salaries, and then pensions. The subsequent priorities include transfers to institutions “according to their social urgency.” All other payments will be made only if funds are available.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_12-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Trade_and_foreign_investment">
        Trade and foreign investment
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Costa Rica has free trade agreements with many countries, including the US. There are no significant trade barriers that would affect imports and the country has been lowering its tariffs in accordance with other Central American countries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
        <a href="#cite_note-94">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The country's Free Trade Zones provide incentives for manufacturing and service industries to operate in Costa Rica. In 2015, the zones supported over 82 thousand direct jobs and 43 thousand indirect jobs in 2015 and average wages in the FTZ were 1.8 times greater than the average for private enterprise work in the rest of the country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_78-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2016,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amazon.com" title="Amazon.com">
        Amazon.com
       </a>
       for example, had some 3,500 employees in Costa Rica and planned to increase that by 1,500 in 2017, making it an important employer.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-seattletimes.com_8-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-seattletimes.com-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The central location provides access to American markets and direct ocean access to Europe and Asia. The most important exports in 2015 (in order of dollar value) were medical instruments, bananas, tropical fruits, integrated circuits and orthopedic appliances.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atlas.media.mit.edu_95-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-atlas.media.mit.edu-95">
         [95]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Total imports in that year were US$15 billion. The most significant products imported in 2015 (in order of dollar value) were refined petroleum, automobiles, packaged medications, broadcasting equipment and computers. The total exports were US$12.6 billion for a trade deficit of US$2.39 billion in 2015.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atlas.media.mit.edu_95-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-atlas.media.mit.edu-95">
         [95]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DirkvdM_orosi_valley_bird.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="852" data-file-width="1136" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/DirkvdM_orosi_valley_bird.jpg/220px-DirkvdM_orosi_valley_bird.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/DirkvdM_orosi_valley_bird.jpg/330px-DirkvdM_orosi_valley_bird.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/DirkvdM_orosi_valley_bird.jpg/440px-DirkvdM_orosi_valley_bird.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DirkvdM_orosi_valley_bird.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A
         <a href="/wiki/Coffee_production_in_Costa_Rica" title="Coffee production in Costa Rica">
          coffee plantation
         </a>
         in the
         <a href="/wiki/Oros%C3%AD" title="Orosí">
          Orosí Valley
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Pharmaceuticals, financial outsourcing, software development, and
       <a href="/wiki/Ecotourism" title="Ecotourism">
        ecotourism
       </a>
       have become the prime industries in Costa Rica's economy. High levels of education among its residents make the country an attractive investing location. Since 1999, tourism earns more foreign exchange than the combined exports of the country's three main
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cash_crops" title="Cash crops">
        cash crops
       </a>
       : bananas and pineapples especially,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-qcostarica.com_96-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-qcostarica.com-96">
         [96]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but also other crops, including coffee.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICT2006_97-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ICT2006-97">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Coffee_production_in_Costa_Rica" title="Coffee production in Costa Rica">
        Coffee production
       </a>
       played a key role in Costa Rica's history and in 2006, was the third cash crop export.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICT2006_97-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ICT2006-97">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As a small country, Costa Rica now provides under 1% of the world’s coffee production.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cafeimports.com_46-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-cafeimports.com-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2015, the value of coffee exports was US$305.9 million, a small part of the total agricultural exports of US$2.7 billion.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-qcostarica.com_96-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-qcostarica.com-96">
         [96]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Coffee production increased by 13.7% percent in 2015-16, declined by 17.5% in 2016-17, but was expected to increase by about 15% in the subsequent year.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
        <a href="#cite_note-98">
         [98]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Costa Rica has developed a system of
       <a href="/wiki/Payment_for_ecosystem_services" title="Payment for ecosystem services">
        payments for environmental services
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI1_63-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-ODI1-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Similarly, Costa Rica has a tax on water pollution to penalize businesses and homeowners that dump sewage, agricultural chemicals, and other pollutants into waterways.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
        <a href="#cite_note-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In May 2007, the Costa Rican government announced its intentions to become 100%
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carbon_neutral" title="Carbon neutral">
        carbon neutral
       </a>
       by 2021.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
        <a href="#cite_note-100">
         [100]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By 2015, 93 percent of the country's electricity came from
       <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy_in_Costa_Rica" title="Renewable energy in Costa Rica">
        renewable sources
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
        <a href="#cite_note-101">
         [101]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2016, the country produced 98% of its electricity from renewable sources and ran completely on renewable sources for 110 continuous days.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
        <a href="#cite_note-102">
         [102]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1996, the Forest Law was enacted to provide direct financial incentives to landowners for the provision of environmental services.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI1_63-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-ODI1-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This helped reorient the forestry sector away from commercial timber production and the resulting
       <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">
        deforestation
       </a>
       , and helped create awareness of the services it provides for the economy and society (i.e.,
       <a href="/wiki/Carbon_fixation" title="Carbon fixation">
        carbon fixation
       </a>
       , hydrological services such as producing fresh drinking water, biodiversity protection, and provision of scenic beauty).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI1_63-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-ODI1-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       A 2016 report by the U.S. government report identifies other challenges facing Costa Rica as it works to expand its economy by working with companies from the US (and probably from other countries).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2016.export.gov_85-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2016.export.gov-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The major concerns identified were as follows:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        The ports, roads, railways and water delivery systems would benefit from major upgrading, a concern voiced by other reports too.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
         <a href="#cite_note-103">
          [103]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Attempts by China to invest in upgrading such aspects were "stalled by bureaucratic and legal concerns".
       </li>
       <li>
        The bureaucracy is "often slow and cumbersome".
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">
        Tourism
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Poas_crater.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Poas_crater.jpg/220px-Poas_crater.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Poas_crater.jpg/330px-Poas_crater.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Poas_crater.jpg/440px-Poas_crater.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Poas_crater.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Po%C3%A1s_Volcano_National_Park" title="Poás Volcano National Park">
          Poás Volcano Crater
         </a>
         is one of the country's main
         <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Costa_Rica" title="Tourism in Costa Rica">
          tourist attractions
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Costa Rica stands as the most visited nation in the Central American region,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Statista_104-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Statista-104">
         [104]
        </a>
       </sup>
       with 2.9 million foreign visitors in 2016, up 10% from 2015.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Central_America_Data_105-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Central_America_Data-105">
         [105]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2012, the tourism sector was responsible for $2.8 million.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LN032013_106-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-LN032013-106">
         [106]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The lead country of origin to enter Costa Rica in 2016 was the United States with 1,000,000 visitors, followed by Europe with 434,884 arrivals.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-El_Financiero_107-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-El_Financiero-107">
         [107]
        </a>
       </sup>
       According to Costa Rica Vacations, once tourists arrive in the country, 22% go to Tamarindo, 18% go to Arenal, 17% pass through
       <a href="/wiki/Liberia,_Costa_Rica" title="Liberia, Costa Rica">
        Liberia
       </a>
       (where the Daniel Oduber Quiros International Airport is located), 16% go to
       <a href="/wiki/San_Jos%C3%A9,_Costa_Rica" title="San José, Costa Rica">
        San José
       </a>
       , the country’s capital (also passing through Juan Santamaria Airport), while 18% chose Manuel Antonio and 7% Monteverde.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Costa_RIca_Vacations_108-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Costa_RIca_Vacations-108">
         [108]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       By 2004, tourism was generating more revenue and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Foreign_exchange_reserves" title="Foreign exchange reserves">
        foreign exchange
       </a>
       than bananas and coffee combined.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ICT2006_97-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-ICT2006-97">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">
        <a href="#cite_note-109">
         [109]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2016, the World Travel &amp; Tourism Council's estimates indicated a direct contribution to the GDP of 5.1% and 110,000 direct jobs in Costa Rica; the total number of jobs indirectly supported by tourism was 271,000.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">
        <a href="#cite_note-110">
         [110]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       A pioneer of
       <a href="/wiki/Ecotourism" title="Ecotourism">
        ecotourism
       </a>
       , Costa Rica draws many tourists to its extensive series of national parks and other protected areas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">
        <a href="#cite_note-111">
         [111]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the 2011
       <a href="/wiki/Travel_and_Tourism_Competitiveness_Report" title="Travel and Tourism Competitiveness Report">
        Travel and Tourism Competitiveness Index
       </a>
       , Costa Rica ranked 44th in the world and second among Latin American countries after Mexico in 2011.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TTCI2011_112-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-TTCI2011-112">
         [112]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By the time of the 2017 report, the country had reached 38th place, slightly behind Panama.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">
        <a href="#cite_note-113">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Ethical Traveler group's ten countries on their 2017 list of The World’s Ten Best Ethical Destinations includes Costa Rica. The country scored highest in environmental protection among the winners.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">
        <a href="#cite_note-114">
         [114]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">
        Governance
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Costa_Rica" title="Politics of Costa Rica">
        Politics of Costa Rica
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">
        Administrative divisions
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Provinces_Costa_Rica.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="317" data-file-width="345" height="202" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Provinces_Costa_Rica.png/220px-Provinces_Costa_Rica.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Provinces_Costa_Rica.png/330px-Provinces_Costa_Rica.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/00/Provinces_Costa_Rica.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Provinces_Costa_Rica.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Provinces of Costa Rica
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Costa_Rica" title="Administrative divisions of Costa Rica">
        Administrative divisions of Costa Rica
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Costa Rica is composed of seven provinces, which in turn are divided into 81 cantons (Spanish:
       <i>
        <span lang="es">
         cantón
        </span>
       </i>
       , plural
       <i>
        <span lang="es">
         <i>
          cantones
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       ), each of which is directed by a mayor. Mayors are chosen democratically every four years by each canton. There are no provincial legislatures. The cantons are further divided into 473 districts (
       <i>
        <span lang="es">
         <i>
          distritos
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       ). The provinces are:
      </p>
      <ol>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Alajuela_Province" title="Alajuela Province">
         Alajuela
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Cartago_Province" title="Cartago Province">
         Cartago
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Guanacaste_Province" title="Guanacaste Province">
         Guanacaste
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Heredia_Province" title="Heredia Province">
         Heredia
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Lim%C3%B3n_Province" title="Limón Province">
         Limón
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Puntarenas_Province" title="Puntarenas Province">
         Puntarenas
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/San_Jos%C3%A9_Province" title="San José Province">
         San José
        </a>
       </li>
      </ol>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">
        Foreign relations
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Costa_Rica" title="Foreign relations of Costa Rica">
        Foreign relations of Costa Rica
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:442px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Localisation_de_l%27ile_de_Clipperton.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="560" data-file-width="790" height="312" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Localisation_de_l%27ile_de_Clipperton.png/440px-Localisation_de_l%27ile_de_Clipperton.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Localisation_de_l%27ile_de_Clipperton.png/660px-Localisation_de_l%27ile_de_Clipperton.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/60/Localisation_de_l%27ile_de_Clipperton.png 2x" width="440"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Localisation_de_l%27ile_de_Clipperton.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The extent of Costa Rica's western
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EEZ" title="EEZ">
          EEZ
         </a>
         in the Pacific.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Barack_Obama_with_Costa_Rican_children.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="436" data-file-width="654" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Barack_Obama_with_Costa_Rican_children.jpg/220px-Barack_Obama_with_Costa_Rican_children.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Barack_Obama_with_Costa_Rican_children.jpg/330px-Barack_Obama_with_Costa_Rican_children.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Barack_Obama_with_Costa_Rican_children.jpg/440px-Barack_Obama_with_Costa_Rican_children.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Barack_Obama_with_Costa_Rican_children.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">
          Barack Obama
         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/Laura_Chinchilla" title="Laura Chinchilla">
          Laura Chinchilla
         </a>
         with Costa Rican children in
         <a href="/wiki/San_Jos%C3%A9,_Costa_Rica" title="San José, Costa Rica">
          San José
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Costa Rica is an active member of the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">
        United Nations
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">
        Organization of American States
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Inter-American_Court_of_Human_Rights" title="Inter-American Court of Human Rights">
        Inter-American Court of Human Rights
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_University_of_Peace" title="United Nations University of Peace">
        United Nations University of Peace
       </a>
       are based in Costa Rica. It is also a member of many other international organizations related to
       <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">
        human rights
       </a>
       and democracy, such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Democracies" title="Community of Democracies">
        Community of Democracies
       </a>
       . A main foreign policy objective of Costa Rica is to foster human rights and sustainable development as a way to secure stability and growth.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">
        <a href="#cite_note-115">
         [115]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Costa Rica is a member of the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Court" title="International Criminal Court">
        International Criminal Court
       </a>
       , without a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bilateral_Immunity_Agreement" title="Bilateral Immunity Agreement">
        Bilateral Immunity Agreement
       </a>
       of protection for the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_military" title="United States military">
        United States military
       </a>
       (as covered under
       <a href="/wiki/Rome_Statute_of_the_International_Criminal_Court" title="Rome Statute of the International Criminal Court">
        Article 98
       </a>
       ). Costa Rica is an observer of the
       <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation internationale de la Francophonie">
        Organisation internationale de la Francophonie
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       On September 10, 1961, some months after
       <a href="/wiki/Fidel_Castro" title="Fidel Castro">
        Fidel Castro
       </a>
       declared
       <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">
        Cuba
       </a>
       a socialist state, Costa Rican President
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mario_Echandi" title="Mario Echandi">
        Mario Echandi
       </a>
       ended diplomatic relations with Cuba through
       <i>
        Executive Decree Number 2
       </i>
       . This freeze lasted 47 years until President
       <a href="/wiki/%C3%93scar_Arias" title="Óscar Arias">
        Óscar Arias Sánchez
       </a>
       re-established normal relations on 18 March 2009, saying, "If we have been able to turn the page with regimes as profoundly different to our reality as occurred with the USSR or, more recently, with the Republic of China, how would we not do it with a country that is geographically and culturally much nearer to Costa Rica?" Arias announced that both countries would exchange ambassadors.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">
        <a href="#cite_note-116">
         [116]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Costa Rica has a long-term disagreement with
       <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">
        Nicaragua
       </a>
       over the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Costa_Rica_%E2%80%93_Nicaragua_San_Juan_River_border_dispute" title="Costa Rica – Nicaragua San Juan River border dispute">
        San Juan River
       </a>
       , which defines the border between the two countries, and Costa Rica's
       <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_navigation" title="Freedom of navigation">
        rights of navigation
       </a>
       on the river.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
        <a href="#cite_note-117">
         [117]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2010, there was also a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Costa_Rica_%E2%80%93_Nicaragua_San_Juan_River_border_dispute#2010_Isla_Calero_dispute" title="Costa Rica – Nicaragua San Juan River border dispute">
        dispute around Isla Calero
       </a>
       , and the impact of Nicaraguan
       <a href="/wiki/Dredging" title="Dredging">
        dredging
       </a>
       of the river in that area.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
        <a href="#cite_note-118">
         [118]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On July 14, 2009, the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">
        International Court of Justice
       </a>
       in the Hague upheld Costa Rica's navigation rights for commercial purposes to
       <a href="/wiki/Artisanal_fishing" title="Artisanal fishing">
        subsistence fishing
       </a>
       on their side of the river. An 1858 treaty extended navigation rights to Costa Rica, but Nicaragua denied passenger travel and fishing were part of the deal; the court ruled Costa Ricans on the river were not required to have Nicaraguan tourist cards or visas as Nicaragua argued, but, in a nod to the Nicaraguans, ruled that Costa Rican boats and passengers must stop at the first and last Nicaraguan port along their route. They must also have an identity document or passport. Nicaragua can also impose timetables on Costa Rican traffic. Nicaragua may require Costa Rican boats to display the
       <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Nicaragua" title="Flag of Nicaragua">
        flag of Nicaragua
       </a>
       , but may not charge them for departure clearance from its ports. These were all specific items of contention brought to the court in the 2005 filing.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">
        <a href="#cite_note-119">
         [119]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On June 1, 2007, Costa Rica broke diplomatic ties with
       <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">
        Taiwan
       </a>
       , switching recognition to the People's Republic of China. Costa Rica was the first of the Central American nations to do so. President
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C3%93scar_Arias_S%C3%A1nchez" title="Óscar Arias Sánchez">
        Óscar Arias Sánchez
       </a>
       admitted the action was a response to economic exigency.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
        <a href="#cite_note-120">
         [120]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In response, the PRC built a new, $100 million, state-of-the-art
       <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">
        football
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Estadio_Nacional_de_Costa_Rica_(2011)" title="Estadio Nacional de Costa Rica (2011)">
        stadium in Parque la Sabana
       </a>
       , in the province of San José. Approximately 600 Chinese engineers and laborers took part in this project, and it was inaugurated in March 2011, with a match between the national teams of
       <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica_national_football_team" title="Costa Rica national football team">
        Costa Rica
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/China_national_football_team" title="China national football team">
        China
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Costa Rica finished a term on the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">
        United Nations Security Council
       </a>
       , having been elected for a nonrenewable, two-year term in the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_election,_2007" title="United Nations Security Council election, 2007">
        2007 election
       </a>
       . Its term expired on December 31, 2009; this was Costa Rica's third time on the Security Council. Elayne Whyte Gómez is the Permanent Representative of Costa Rica to the UN Office at Geneva (2017) and President of the United Nations Conference to Negotiate a Legally Binding Instrument to Prohibit Nuclear Weapons.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
        <a href="#cite_note-121">
         [121]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">
        Demographics
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Costa_Rica" title="Demographics of Costa Rica">
        Demographics of Costa Rica
       </a>
      </div>
      <table class="wikitable collapsible collapsed" style="float: right; margin: 0 0.5em 0 2em;">
       <tr>
        <th colspan="3">
         Costa Rican Censuses
        </th>
       </tr>

       </tr>

        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica_2011_Census" title="Costa Rica 2011 Census">
          2011
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         4,301,712
        </td>
        <td>
         12.9
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica_2011_Census" title="Costa Rica 2011 Census">
        2011 census
       </a>
       counted a population of 4.3 million people
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
        <a href="#cite_note-122">
         [122]
        </a>
       </sup>
       distributed among the following groups: 83.6% whites or
       <a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">
        mestizos
       </a>
       , 6.7%
       <a href="/wiki/Mulatto" title="Mulatto">
        mulattoes
       </a>
       , 2.4%
       <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">
        Native American
       </a>
       , 1.1% black or
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afro-Costa_Rican" title="Afro-Costa Rican">
        Afro-Caribbean
       </a>
       ; the census showed 1.1% as Other, 2.9% (141,304 people) as None, and 2.2% (107,196 people) as unspecified.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-livepopulation.com_1-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-livepopulation.com-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By 2016, the UN estimation for the population was around 4.9 million.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_3-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2011, there were over 104,000 Native American or indigenous inhabitants, representing 2.4% of the population. Most of them live in secluded reservations, distributed among eight ethnic groups:
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Quitirris%C3%AD&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Quitirrisí (page does not exist)">
        Quitirrisí
       </a>
       <span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">
        (
        <a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quitirris%C3%AD" title="es:Quitirrisí">
         es
        </a>
        )
       </span>
       (in the Central Valley), Matambú or
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chorotega_people" title="Chorotega people">
        Chorotega
       </a>
       (Guanacaste),
       <a href="/wiki/Maleku_people" title="Maleku people">
        Maleku
       </a>
       (northern Alajuela),
       <a href="/wiki/Bribri_people" title="Bribri people">
        Bribri
       </a>
       (southern Atlantic),
       <a href="/wiki/Cab%C3%A9car_people" title="Cabécar people">
        Cabécar
       </a>
       (Cordillera de Talamanca), [[]] (southern Costa Rica, along the Panamá border),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boruca_people" title="Boruca people">
        Boruca
       </a>
       (southern Costa Rica) and
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=T%C3%A9rraba&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Térraba (page does not exist)">
        Térraba
       </a>
       <span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">
        (
        <a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/T%C3%A9rraba" title="es:Térraba">
         es
        </a>
        )
       </span>
       (southern Costa Rica).
      </p>
      <p>
       The population includes
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Costa_Ricans" title="European Costa Ricans">
        European Costa Ricans
       </a>
       (of European ancestry), primarily of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_people" title="Spanish people">
        Spanish
       </a>
       descent,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_2-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-CIA-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       with significant numbers of Italian, German, English, Dutch, French, Irish, Portuguese, and Polish families, as well a sizable Jewish community. The majority of the Afro-Costa Ricans are
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Creole_English" title="Creole English">
        Creole English
       </a>
       -speaking descendants of 19th century black
       <a href="/wiki/Jamaicans" title="Jamaicans">
        Jamaican
       </a>
       immigrant workers.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ni%C3%B1os_costarricenses.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="422" data-file-width="545" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Ni%C3%B1os_costarricenses.JPG/220px-Ni%C3%B1os_costarricenses.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Ni%C3%B1os_costarricenses.JPG/330px-Ni%C3%B1os_costarricenses.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Ni%C3%B1os_costarricenses.JPG/440px-Ni%C3%B1os_costarricenses.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ni%C3%B1os_costarricenses.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Costa Rican school children
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The 2011 census classified 83.6% of the population as white or
       <a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">
        Mestizo
       </a>
       ; the latter are persons of combined European and Amerindian descent. The
       <a href="/wiki/Mulatto" title="Mulatto">
        Mulatto
       </a>
       segment (mix of white and black) represented 6.7% and indigenous people made up 2.4% of the population.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_2-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-CIA-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Native and European mixed blood populations are far less than in other Latin American countries. Exceptions are
       <a href="/wiki/Guanacaste_Province" title="Guanacaste Province">
        Guanacaste
       </a>
       , where almost half the population is visibly mestizo, a legacy of the more pervasive unions between Spanish colonists and Chorotega Amerindians through several generations, and
       <a href="/wiki/Lim%C3%B3n" title="Limón">
        Limón
       </a>
       , where the vast majority of the Afro-Costa Rican community lives.
      </p>
      <p>
       Costa Rica hosts many refugees, mainly from
       <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">
        Colombia
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">
        Nicaragua
       </a>
       . As a result of that and illegal immigration, an estimated 10–15% (400,000–600,000) of the Costa Rican population is made up of Nicaraguans.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">
        <a href="#cite_note-123">
         [123]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">
        <a href="#cite_note-124">
         [124]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Some Nicaraguans migrate for seasonal work opportunities and then return to their country. Costa Rica took in many refugees from a range of other Latin American countries fleeing civil wars and dictatorships during the 1970s and 1980s, notably from
       <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">
        Chile
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">
        Argentina
       </a>
       , as well as people from
       <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador" title="El Salvador">
        El Salvador
       </a>
       who fled from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guerrillas" title="Guerrillas">
        guerrillas
       </a>
       and government
       <a href="/wiki/Death_squad" title="Death squad">
        death squads
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">
        <a href="#cite_note-125">
         [125]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       According to the
       <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">
        World Bank
       </a>
       , in 2010 about 489,200 immigrants lived in the country, many from Nicaragua, Panama, El Salvador, Honduras, Guatemala, and Belize, while 125,306 Costa Ricans live abroad in the United States, Panama, Nicaragua, Spain, Mexico, Canada, Germany, Venezuela,
       <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">
        Dominican Republic
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">
        Ecuador
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">
        <a href="#cite_note-126">
         [126]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The number of migrants declined in later years but in 2015, there were some 420,000 immigrants in Costa Rica
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">
        <a href="#cite_note-127">
         [127]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the number of asylum seekers (mostly from Honduras, El Salvador, Guatemala and Nicaragua) rose to more than 110,000, a fivefold increase from 2012.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">
        <a href="#cite_note-128">
         [128]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2016, the country was called a "magnet" for migrants from South and Central America and other countries who were hoping to reach the U.S.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129">
        <a href="#cite_note-129">
         [129]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130">
        <a href="#cite_note-130">
         [130]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
