      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">
        Religion
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright" style="">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:200px">
        <div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black">
         <div class="transborder" style="position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 15915.284869156px; border-left-color:Red">
         </div>
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Red">
         </div>
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Red">
         </div>
         <div class="transborder" style="position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 687.15418461369px; border-left-color:Gold">
         </div>
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Gold">
         </div>
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Gold">
         </div>
         <div class="transborder" style="position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 352.45314152574px; border-left-color:Gray">
         </div>
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Gray">
         </div>
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Gray">
         </div>
         <div class="transborder" style="position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 66.138368814878px; border-left-color:DarkOrchid">
         </div>
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:DarkOrchid">
         </div>
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:DarkOrchid">
         </div>
         <div class="transborder" style="position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;right:100px; top:100px; border-width:96.029368567694px 27.899110603923px 0 0; border-top-color:DodgerBlue">
         </div>
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:DodgerBlue">
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <p>
          Religion in Costa Rica
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-report_131-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-report-131">
            [131]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-buddhistchannel.tv_132-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-buddhistchannel.tv-132">
            [132]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DodgerBlue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">
           Catholicism
          </a>
          (70.5%)
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DarkOrchid; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">
           Protestantism
          </a>
          (13.8%)
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Gray; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          <a href="/wiki/Irreligion" title="Irreligion">
           Irreligion
          </a>
          (11.3%)
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Gold; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">
           Buddhism
          </a>
          (2.1%)
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Red; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Other religions (2.2%)
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Costa_Rica" title="Religion in Costa Rica">
        Religion in Costa Rica
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Basilica_de_los_Angeles_2007.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Basilica_de_los_Angeles_2007.jpg/220px-Basilica_de_los_Angeles_2007.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Basilica_de_los_Angeles_2007.jpg/330px-Basilica_de_los_Angeles_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Basilica_de_los_Angeles_2007.jpg/440px-Basilica_de_los_Angeles_2007.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Basilica_de_los_Angeles_2007.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Basílica de Nuestra Señora de los Ángeles (Basilica of Our Lady of the Angels), during 2007 pilgrimage
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Christianity is Costa Rica's predominant religion, with
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" title="Roman Catholicism">
        Roman Catholicism
       </a>
       being the official
       <a href="/wiki/State_religion" title="State religion">
        state religion
       </a>
       according to the 1949 Constitution, which at the same time guarantees
       <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion" title="Freedom of religion">
        freedom of religion
       </a>
       . It is the only state in the
       <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">
        Americas
       </a>
       which established Roman Catholicism as its state religion; other such countries are microstates in Europe:
       <a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein" title="Liechtenstein">
        Liechtenstein
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">
        Monaco
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">
        Vatican City
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">
        Malta
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       According to the most recent nationwide survey of religion, conducted in 2007 by the
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Costa_Rica" title="University of Costa Rica">
        University of Costa Rica
       </a>
       , 70.5% of Costa Ricans are Roman Catholics (44.9% practicing Catholics), 13.8% are
       <a href="/wiki/Evangelicalism" title="Evangelicalism">
        Evangelical Protestants
       </a>
       (almost all are practicing), 11.3% report that they do not have a religion, and 4.3% belong to another religion. The rate of secularism is high by Latin American standards.
      </p>
      <p>
       Due to small, but continuous, immigration from Asia and the Middle East, other religions have grown, the most popular being
       <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">
        Buddhism
       </a>
       , with about 100,000 practitioners (over 2% of the population).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-buddhistchannel.tv_132-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-buddhistchannel.tv-132">
         [132]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Most Buddhists are members of the
       <a href="/wiki/Han_Chinese" title="Han Chinese">
        Han Chinese
       </a>
       community of about 40,000 with some new local converts. There is also a small
       <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Costa_Rica" title="Islam in Costa Rica">
        Muslim
       </a>
       community of about 500 families, or 0.001% of the population.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133">
        <a href="#cite_note-133">
         [133]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Sinagoga Shaarei Zion synagogue
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134">
        <a href="#cite_note-134">
         [134]
        </a>
       </sup>
       is near
       <a href="/wiki/La_Sabana_Metropolitan_Park" title="La Sabana Metropolitan Park">
        La Sabana Metropolitan Park
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/San_Jos%C3%A9,_Costa_Rica" title="San José, Costa Rica">
        San José
       </a>
       . Several homes in the neighborhood east of the park display the
       <a href="/wiki/Star_of_David" title="Star of David">
        Star of David
       </a>
       and other Jewish symbols.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135">
        <a href="#cite_note-135">
         [135]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">
        The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints
       </a>
       claims more than 35,000 members, and has a
       <a href="/wiki/San_Jos%C3%A9_Costa_Rica_Temple" title="San José Costa Rica Temple">
        temple in San José
       </a>
       that served as a regional worship center for Costa Rica.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136">
        <a href="#cite_note-136">
         [136]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, they represent less than 1% of the population.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">
        <a href="#cite_note-137">
         [137]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138">
        <a href="#cite_note-138">
         [138]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">
        Languages
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Costa_Rica" title="Languages of Costa Rica">
        Languages of Costa Rica
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The primary language spoken in Costa Rica is
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       , which features characteristics
       <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rican_Spanish" title="Costa Rican Spanish">
        distinct to the country
       </a>
       , a form of Central American Spanish. Costa Rica is a linguistically diverse country and home to at least five living local indigenous languages spoken by the descendants of pre-Columbian peoples: Maléku, Cabécar, Bribri, Guaymí, and Buglere.
      </p>
      <p>
       Of native languages still spoken, primarily in indigenous reservations, the most numerically important are the
       <a href="/wiki/Bribri_language" title="Bribri language">
        Bribri
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mal%C3%A9ku_language" title="Maléku language">
        Maléku
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cab%C3%A9car_language" title="Cabécar language">
        Cabécar
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ng%C3%A4bere_language" title="Ngäbere language">
        Ngäbere languages
       </a>
       ; some of these have several thousand speakers in Costa Rica while others have a few hundred. Some languages, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Teribe_language" title="Teribe language">
        Teribe
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Boruca_language" title="Boruca language">
        Boruca
       </a>
       , have fewer than a thousand speakers. The Buglere language and the closely related Guaymí are spoken by some in southeast Puntarenas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-worldatlas.com_139-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-worldatlas.com-139">
         [139]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       A
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English-based_creole_language" title="English-based creole language">
        Creole-English
       </a>
       language,
       <a href="/wiki/Jamaican_Patois" title="Jamaican Patois">
        Jamaican
        <i>
         patois
        </i>
       </a>
       (also known as
       <a href="/wiki/Limonese_Creole" title="Limonese Creole">
        Mekatelyu
       </a>
       ), is an English-based Creole language spoken by the Afro-Carib immigrants who have settled primarily in Limón Province along the Caribbean coast.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-worldatlas.com_139-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-worldatlas.com-139">
         [139]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       About 10.7% of Costa Rica's adult population (18 or older) also speaks English, 0.7% French, and 0.3% speaks
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">
        Portuguese
       </a>
       or German as a second language.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140">
        <a href="#cite_note-140">
         [140]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">
        Culture
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gallo_Pinto_at_breakfast.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="673" data-file-width="900" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Gallo_Pinto_at_breakfast.jpg/220px-Gallo_Pinto_at_breakfast.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Gallo_Pinto_at_breakfast.jpg/330px-Gallo_Pinto_at_breakfast.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Gallo_Pinto_at_breakfast.jpg/440px-Gallo_Pinto_at_breakfast.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gallo_Pinto_at_breakfast.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Costa Rican breakfast with
         <a href="/wiki/Gallo_pinto" title="Gallo pinto">
          gallo pinto
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:World%27s_Largest_Oxcart_Sarchi_Costa_Rica.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/World%27s_Largest_Oxcart_Sarchi_Costa_Rica.JPG/220px-World%27s_Largest_Oxcart_Sarchi_Costa_Rica.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/World%27s_Largest_Oxcart_Sarchi_Costa_Rica.JPG/330px-World%27s_Largest_Oxcart_Sarchi_Costa_Rica.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/World%27s_Largest_Oxcart_Sarchi_Costa_Rica.JPG/440px-World%27s_Largest_Oxcart_Sarchi_Costa_Rica.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:World%27s_Largest_Oxcart_Sarchi_Costa_Rica.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Las_Carretas,_Costa_Rican_Oxcarts" title="Las Carretas, Costa Rican Oxcarts">
          Las Carretas (oxcarts)
         </a>
         are a national symbol.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Costa_Rica" title="Culture of Costa Rica">
        Culture of Costa Rica
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Costa Rica was the point where the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mesoamerican" title="Mesoamerican">
        Mesoamerican
       </a>
       and South American native cultures met. The northwest of the country, the Nicoya peninsula, was the southernmost point of
       <a href="/wiki/Nahuatl" title="Nahuatl">
        Nahuatl
       </a>
       cultural influence when the Spanish conquerors (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conquistadores" title="Conquistadores">
        conquistadores
       </a>
       ) came in the 16th century. The central and southern portions of the country had
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chibcha" title="Chibcha">
        Chibcha
       </a>
       influences. The Atlantic coast, meanwhile, was populated with African workers during the 17th and 18th centuries.
      </p>
      <p>
       As a result of the immigration of Spaniards, their 16th-century Spanish culture and its evolution marked everyday life and culture until today, with Spanish language and the Catholic religion as primary influences.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Department of Culture, Youth, and Sports is in charge of the promotion and coordination of cultural life. The work of the department is divided into Direction of Culture, Visual Arts, Scenic Arts, Music, Patrimony and the System of Libraries. Permanent programs, such as the National Symphony Orchestra of Costa Rica and the Youth Symphony Orchestra, are conjunctions of two areas of work: Culture and Youth.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2009)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Dance-oriented genres, such as
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Soca_music" title="Soca music">
         soca
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Salsa_music" title="Salsa music">
         salsa
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Bachata_(music)" title="Bachata (music)">
         bachata
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Merengue_music" title="Merengue music">
         merengue
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Cumbia" title="Cumbia">
         cumbia
        </a>
       </i>
       and Costa Rican swing are enjoyed increasingly by older rather than younger people. The guitar is popular, especially as an accompaniment to folk dances; however, the marimba was made the national instrument.
      </p>
      <p>
       In November 2017,
       <a href="/wiki/National_Geographic" title="National Geographic">
        National Geographic
       </a>
       magazine named Costa Rica as the happiest country in the world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141">
        <a href="#cite_note-141">
         [141]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The article included this summary: "Costa Ricans enjoy the pleasure of living daily life to the fullest in a place that mitigates stress and maximizes joy".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142">
        <a href="#cite_note-142">
         [142]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is not surprising then that one of the most recognizable phrases among "Ticos" is "
       <i>
        Pura Vida
       </i>
       ", pure life in a literal translation. It reflects the inhabitant's philosophy of life,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-elementonatural.com_143-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-elementonatural.com-143">
         [143]
        </a>
       </sup>
       denoting a simple life, free of stress, a positive, relaxed feeling.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144">
        <a href="#cite_note-144">
         [144]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The expression is used in various contexts in conversation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145">
        <a href="#cite_note-145">
         [145]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Often, people walking down the streets, or buying food at shops say hello by saying
       <i>
        Pura Vida
       </i>
       . It can be phrased as a question or as an acknowledgement of one's presence. A recommended response to "How are you?" would be "
       <i>
        Pura Vida
       </i>
       ."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146">
        <a href="#cite_note-146">
         [146]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In that usage, it might be translated as "awesome", indicating that all is very well
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147">
        <a href="#cite_note-147">
         [147]
        </a>
       </sup>
       . When used as a question, the connotation would be "everything is going well?" or "how are you?".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-elementonatural.com_143-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-elementonatural.com-143">
         [143]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Costa Rica rates 12th on the 2017
       <a href="/wiki/Happy_Planet_Index" title="Happy Planet Index">
        Happy Planet Index
       </a>
       in the World Happiness Report by the UN
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148">
        <a href="#cite_note-148">
         [148]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but the country is said to be the happiest in Latin America. Reasons include the high level of social services, the caring nature of its inhabitants, long life expectancy and relatively low corruption.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149">
        <a href="#cite_note-149">
         [149]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150">
        <a href="#cite_note-150">
         [150]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">
        Cuisine
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rican_cuisine" title="Costa Rican cuisine">
        Costa Rican cuisine
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Costa Rican cuisine is a blend of
       <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">
        Native American
       </a>
       , Spanish, African and many other cuisine origins. Dishes such as the very traditional
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tamal_(dish)" title="Tamal (dish)">
        tamale
       </a>
       and many others made of corn are the most representative of its indigenous inhabitants, and similar to other neighboring Mesoamerican countries. Spaniards brought many new ingredients to the country from other lands, especially spices and domestic animals. And later in the 19th century, the African flavor lent its presence with influence from other Caribbean mixed flavors. This is how Costa Rican cuisine today is very varied, with every new ethnic group who had recently become part of the country's population influencing the country's cuisine.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151">
        <a href="#cite_note-151">
         [151]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources">
          <span title="The material near this tag may rely on an unreliable source. (February 2011)">
           unreliable source?
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">
        Sports
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica_at_the_Olympics" title="Costa Rica at the Olympics">
        Costa Rica at the Olympics
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Association_football_in_Costa_Rica" title="Association football in Costa Rica">
        Association football in Costa Rica
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Claudia_Poll.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="361" data-file-width="240" height="331" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Claudia_Poll.jpg/220px-Claudia_Poll.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7b/Claudia_Poll.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Claudia_Poll.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Claudia_Poll" title="Claudia Poll">
          Claudia Poll
         </a>
         won Costa Rica's first Olympic gold medal in 1996.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Costa Rica entered the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Summer_Olympics" title="Summer Olympics">
        Summer Olympics
       </a>
       for the first time in 1936 with the fencer
       <a href="/wiki/Bernardo_de_la_Guardia" title="Bernardo de la Guardia">
        Bernardo de la Guardia
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Winter_Olympics" title="Winter Olympics">
        Winter Olympics
       </a>
       for the first time in 1980 with the skier
       <a href="/wiki/Arturo_Kinch" title="Arturo Kinch">
        Arturo Kinch
       </a>
       . All four of Costa Rica's Olympic medals were won by the sisters
       <a href="/wiki/Silvia_Poll" title="Silvia Poll">
        Silvia
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Claudia_Poll" title="Claudia Poll">
        Claudia Poll
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Swimming_(sport)" title="Swimming (sport)">
        swimming
       </a>
       , with Claudia winning the only gold medal in
       <a href="/wiki/Swimming_at_the_1996_Summer_Olympics" title="Swimming at the 1996 Summer Olympics">
        1996
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Football is the most popular sport in Costa Rica. The
       <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica_national_football_team" title="Costa Rica national football team">
        national team
       </a>
       has played in four
       <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">
        FIFA World Cup
       </a>
       tournaments and reached the quarter-finals for the first time in
       <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">
        2014
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152">
        <a href="#cite_note-152">
         [152]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153">
        <a href="#cite_note-153">
         [153]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Its best performance in the regional
       <a href="/wiki/CONCACAF_Gold_Cup" title="CONCACAF Gold Cup">
        CONCACAF Gold Cup
       </a>
       was runner-up in
       <a href="/wiki/2002_CONCACAF_Gold_Cup" title="2002 CONCACAF Gold Cup">
        2002
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Paulo_Wanchope" title="Paulo Wanchope">
        Paulo Wanchope
       </a>
       , a forward who played for three clubs in England's
       <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">
        Premier League
       </a>
       in the late 1990s and early 2000s, is credited with enhancing foreign recognition of Costa Rican football.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2018)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">
        Education
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Costa_Rica" title="Education in Costa Rica">
        Education in Costa Rica
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The literacy rate in Costa Rica is approximately 97 percent and English is widely spoken primarily due to Costa Rica’s tourism industry.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2016.export.gov_85-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-2016.export.gov-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
       When the army was abolished in 1949, it was said that the "army would be replaced with an army of teachers".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154">
        <a href="#cite_note-154">
         [154]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Universal
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_education" title="Public education">
        public education
       </a>
       is guaranteed in the constitution; primary education is obligatory, and both preschool and high school are free. Students who finish 11th grade receive a Costa Rican Bachillerato Diploma accredited by the Costa Rican Ministry of Education.
      </p>
      <p>
       There are both state and private universities. The
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Costa_Rica" title="University of Costa Rica">
        University of Costa Rica
       </a>
       has been awarded the title "Meritorious Institution of Costa Rican Education and Culture".
      </p>
      <p>
       A 2016 report by the U.S. government report identifies the current challenges facing the education system, including the high dropout rate among high school students. The country needs even more workers who are fluent in English and languages such as Portuguese, Mandarin and French. It would also benefit from more graduates in Science, Technology, Engineering and Math (STEM) programs, according to the report.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2016.export.gov_85-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-2016.export.gov-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Health">
        Health
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Health_care_in_Costa_Rica" title="Health care in Costa Rica">
        Health care in Costa Rica
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       According to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNDP" title="UNDP">
        UNDP
       </a>
       , in 2010 the
       <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">
        life expectancy
       </a>
       at birth for Costa Ricans was 79.3 years.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155">
        <a href="#cite_note-155">
         [155]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Nicoya_Peninsula" title="Nicoya Peninsula">
        Nicoya Peninsula
       </a>
       is considered one of the
       <a href="/wiki/Blue_Zone" title="Blue Zone">
        Blue Zones
       </a>
       in the world, where people commonly live active lives past the age of 100 years.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156">
        <a href="#cite_note-156">
         [156]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157">
        <a href="#cite_note-157">
         [157]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/New_Economics_Foundation" title="New Economics Foundation">
        New Economics Foundation
       </a>
       (NEF) ranked Costa Rica first in its 2009
       <a href="/wiki/Happy_Planet_Index" title="Happy Planet Index">
        Happy Planet Index
       </a>
       , and once again in 2012. The index measures the health and happiness they produce per unit of environmental input.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HPI01_22-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-HPI01-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HPI02_23-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-HPI02-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       According to NEF, Costa Rica's lead is due to its very high
       <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">
        life expectancy
       </a>
       which is second highest in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Americas" title="The Americas">
        the Americas
       </a>
       , and higher than the United States. The country also experienced well-being higher than many richer nations and a per capita
       <a href="/wiki/Ecological_footprint" title="Ecological footprint">
        ecological footprint
       </a>
       one-third the size of the United States.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158">
        <a href="#cite_note-158">
         [158]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2002, there were 0.58 new general practitioner (medical) consultations and 0.33 new specialist consultations per capita, and a hospital admission rate of 8.1%. Preventive health care is also successful. In 2002, 96% of Costa Rican women used some form of contraception, and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antenatal_care" title="Antenatal care">
        antenatal care
       </a>
       services were provided to 87% of all pregnant women. All children under one have access to well-baby clinics, and the immunization coverage rate in 2002 was above 91% for all antigens.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2011)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Costa Rica has a very low
       <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">
        malaria
       </a>
       incidence of 48 per 100,000 in 2000 and no reported cases of
       <a href="/wiki/Measles" title="Measles">
        measles
       </a>
       in 2002. The perinatal mortality rate dropped from 12.0 per 1000 in 1972 to 5.4 per 1000 in 2001.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159">
        <a href="#cite_note-159">
         [159]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Costa Rica has been cited in various journals as Central America's great health success story.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2010)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Its healthcare system is ranked higher than that of the United States, despite having a fraction of its GDP.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160">
        <a href="#cite_note-160">
         [160]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Prior to 1940, government hospitals and charities provided most health care. But since the 1941 creation of the Social Insurance Administration (
       <i>
        Caja Costarricense de Seguro Social
       </i>
       – CCSS), Costa Rica has provided
       <a href="/wiki/Universal_health_care" title="Universal health care">
        universal health care
       </a>
       to its wage-earning residents, with coverage extended to dependants over time. In 1973, the CCSS took over administration of all 29 of the country's public hospitals and all health care, also launching a Rural Health Program (
       <i>
        Programa de Salud Rural
       </i>
       ) for primary care to rural areas, later extended to primary care services nationwide. In 1993, laws were passed to enable elected health boards that represented health consumers, social insurance representatives, employers, and social organizations. By the year 2000, social health insurance coverage was available to 82% of the Costa Rican population. Each health committee manages an area equivalent to one of the 83 administrative cantons of Costa Rica. There is limited use of private, for-profit services (around 14.4% of the national total health expenditure). About 7% of GDP is allocated to the health sector, and over 70% is government funded.
      </p>
      <p>
       Primary health care facilities in Costa Rica include health clinics, with a
       <a href="/wiki/General_practitioner" title="General practitioner">
        general practitioner
       </a>
       , nurse, clerk, pharmacist and a primary health technician. In 2008, there were five specialty national hospitals, three general national hospitals, seven regional hospitals, 13 peripheral hospitals, and 10 major clinics serving as referral centers for primary care clinics, which also deliver biopsychosocial services, family and community medical services and promotion and prevention programs. Patients can choose private health care to avoid waiting lists.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2011)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Costa Rica is among the Latin America countries that have become popular destinations for
       <a href="/wiki/Medical_tourism" title="Medical tourism">
        medical tourism
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Herrick_161-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Herrick-161">
         [161]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bookman_162-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Bookman-162">
         [162]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2006, Costa Rica received 150,000 foreigners that came for medical treatment.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Herrick_161-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Herrick-161">
         [161]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bookman_162-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Bookman-162">
         [162]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stats_163-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Stats-163">
         [163]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Costa Rica is particularly attractive to Americans due to geographic proximity, high quality of medical services, and lower medical costs.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bookman_162-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Bookman-162">
         [162]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Since 2012,
       <a href="/wiki/Smoking_in_Costa_Rica" title="Smoking in Costa Rica">
        smoking in Costa Rica
       </a>
       is subject to some of the most restrictive regulations in the world.
      </p>
